<p>Andalusia is traditionally divided into two historical subregions: <b><i>Upper Andalusia</i> or <i>Eastern Andalusia</i></b> (<i>Andalucía Oriental</i>), consisting of the provinces of Almería, Granada, Jaén, and Málaga, and <b><i>Lower Andalusia</i> or <i>Western Andalusia</i></b> (<i>Andalucía Occidental</i>), consisting of the provinces of Cádiz, Córdoba, Huelva and Seville.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities_and_local_entities">Municipalities and local entities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Municipalities and local entities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andalucia_municipalities.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1395" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Andalucia_municipalities.png/325px-Andalucia_municipalities.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Andalucia_municipalities.png/488px-Andalucia_municipalities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Andalucia_municipalities.png/650px-Andalucia_municipalities.png 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andalucia_municipalities.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Municipalities of Andalusia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beyond the level of provinces, Andalusia is further divided into 774 <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_Spain" title="List of municipalities of Spain">municipalities</a> (<i>municipios</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-del_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-del-72">[72]</a></sup> The municipalities of Andalusia are regulated by Title III of the Statute of Autonomy, Articles 91–95, which establishes the municipality as the basic territorial entity of Andalusia, each of which has legal personhood and autonomy in many aspects of its internal affairs. At the municipal level, representation, government and administration is performed by the <i>ayuntamiento</i> (municipal government), which has competency for <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a>, community social services, supply and treatment of water, collection and treatment of waste, and promotion of tourism, culture, and sports, among other matters established by law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the more important Andalusian cities besides the provincial capitals are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/El_Ejido" title="El Ejido">El Ejido</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%ADjar" title="Níjar">Níjar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roquetas_de_Mar" title="Roquetas de Mar">Roquetas de Mar</a> (Almería)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La Línea de la Concepción">La Línea de la Concepción</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">Algeciras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanl%C3%BAcar_de_Barrameda" title="Sanlúcar de Barrameda">Sanlúcar de Barrameda</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_C%C3%A1diz" title="San Fernando, Cádiz">San Fernando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiclana_de_la_Frontera" title="Chiclana de la Frontera">Chiclana de la Frontera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Real" title="Puerto Real">Puerto Real</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcos_de_la_Frontera" title="Arcos de la Frontera">Arcos de la Frontera</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerez" title="Jerez">Jerez</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Puerto_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa" title="El Puerto de Santa María">El Puerto de Santa María</a> (Cádiz)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lucena,_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Lucena, Córdoba">Lucena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pozoblanco" title="Pozoblanco">Pozoblanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montilla" title="Montilla">Montilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puente_Genil" title="Puente Genil">Puente Genil</a> (Córdoba)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Almu%C3%B1%C3%A9car" title="Almuñécar">Almuñécar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadix" title="Guadix">Guadix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loja,_Granada" title="Loja, Granada">Loja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motril" title="Motril">Motril</a> (Granada)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Linares,_Ja%C3%A9n" title="Linares, Jaén">Linares</a>, <a href="/wiki/And%C3%BAjar" title="Andújar">Andújar</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Abeda" title="Úbeda">Úbeda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baeza" title="Baeza">Baeza</a> (Jaén)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marbella" title="Marbella">Marbella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mijas" title="Mijas">Mijas</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9lez-M%C3%A1laga" title="Vélez-Málaga">Vélez-Málaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuengirola" title="Fuengirola">Fuengirola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torremolinos" title="Torremolinos">Torremolinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estepona" title="Estepona">Estepona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benalm%C3%A1dena" title="Benalmádena">Benalmádena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antequera" title="Antequera">Antequera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n_de_la_Victoria" title="Rincón de la Victoria">Rincón de la Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronda" title="Ronda">Ronda</a> (Málaga)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Utrera" title="Utrera">Utrera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dos_Hermanas" title="Dos Hermanas">Dos Hermanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Guada%C3%ADra" title="Alcalá de Guadaíra">Alcalá de Guadaíra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osuna" title="Osuna">Osuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mairena_del_Aljarafe" title="Mairena del Aljarafe">Mairena del Aljarafe</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cija" title="Écija">Écija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebrija" title="Lebrija">Lebrija</a> (Sevilla)</li>
</ul>
<p>In conformity with the intent to devolve control as locally as possible, in many cases, separate nuclei of population within municipal borders each administer their own interests. These are variously known as <i>pedanías</i> ("hamlets"), <i>villas</i> ("villages"), <i>aldeas</i> (also usually rendered as "villages"), or other similar names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-del_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-del-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comarcas_and_mancomunidades">Comarcas and mancomunidades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Comarcas and mancomunidades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Andalusia.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="1024" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Regions_of_Andalusia.svg/325px-Regions_of_Andalusia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Regions_of_Andalusia.svg/488px-Regions_of_Andalusia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Regions_of_Andalusia.svg/650px-Regions_of_Andalusia.svg.png 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Andalusia.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Comarcas_of_Andalusia" title="Comarcas of Andalusia">Comarcas of Andalusia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Within the various autonomous communities of Spain, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comarcas" title="Comarcas">comarcas</a></i> are comparable to <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shires</a> (or, in some countries, <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">counties</a>) in the English-speaking world. Unlike in some of Spain's other autonomous communities, under the original 1981 Statute of Autonomy, the <a href="/wiki/Comarcas_of_Andalusia" title="Comarcas of Andalusia"><i>comarcas</i> of Andalusia</a> had no formal recognition, but, in practice, they still had informal recognition as geographic, cultural, historical, or in some cases administrative entities. The 2007 Statute of Autonomy echoes this practice, and mentions <i>comarcas</i> in Article 97 of Title III, which defines the significance of <i>comarcas</i> and establishes a basis for formal recognition in future legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current statutory entity that most closely resembles a <i>comarca</i> is the <i><a href="/wiki/Mancomunidad" title="Mancomunidad">mancomunidad</a></i>, a freely chosen, bottom-up association of municipalities intended as an instrument of socioeconomic development and coordination between municipal governments in specific areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-del_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-del-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Andalusia ranks first by population among the 17 autonomous communities of Spain. The estimated population at the beginning of 2009 was 8,285,692.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEpob2008_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEpob2008-77">[77]</a></sup> The population is concentrated, above all, in the provincial capitals and along the coasts, so that the level of urbanization is quite high; half the population is concentrated in the 28 cities of more than 50,000 inhabitants. The population is aging, although the process of immigration is countering the inversion of the <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p>At the end of the 20th century, Andalusia was in the last phase of <a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">demographic transition</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_rate" title="Death rate">death rate</a> stagnated at around 8–9 per thousand, and the population came to be influenced mainly by birth and migration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pob2_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-pob2-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poblacion_andalucia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1654" data-file-width="2340" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Poblacion_andalucia.png/300px-Poblacion_andalucia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Poblacion_andalucia.png/450px-Poblacion_andalucia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Poblacion_andalucia.png/600px-Poblacion_andalucia.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poblacion_andalucia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population by municipalities in Andalusia in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEpob2007_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEpob2007-81">[81]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1950, Andalusia had 20.04 percent of the national population of Spain. By 1981, this had declined to 17.09 percent. Although the Andalusian population was not declining in absolute terms, these relative losses were due to emigration great enough to nearly counterbalance having the highest <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> in Spain. Since the 1980s, this process has reversed on all counts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Llanes_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Llanes-82">[82]</a></sup> and as of 2009, Andalusia has 17.82 percent of the Spanish population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pob_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-pob-83">[83]</a></sup> The birth rate is sharply down, as is typical in developed economies, although it has lagged behind much of the rest of the world in this respect. Furthermore, prior emigrants have been returning to Andalusia. Beginning in the 1990s, others have been immigrating in large numbers as well, as Spain has become a country of net immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Llanes_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Llanes-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the 21st century, statistics show a slight increase in the birth rate, due in large part to the higher birth rate among immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indicadores_sociales_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indicadores_sociales-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pob_Extranjera_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pob_Extranjera-85">[85]</a></sup> The result is that as of 2009, the trend toward rejuvenation of the population is among the strongest of any autonomous community of Spain, or of any comparable region in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pob_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-pob-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nat_mor_anda.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="1030" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nat_mor_anda.png/220px-Nat_mor_anda.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nat_mor_anda.png/330px-Nat_mor_anda.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Nat_mor_anda.png/440px-Nat_mor_anda.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nat_mor_anda.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Evolution of the birth and death rates of Andalusia 1975–2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andalucia_piramide.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="561" data-file-width="950" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Andalucia_piramide.PNG/220px-Andalucia_piramide.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Andalucia_piramide.PNG/330px-Andalucia_piramide.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Andalucia_piramide.PNG/440px-Andalucia_piramide.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andalucia_piramide.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Structure of the population of Andalusia by sex and age. 2008 data 2008; 1986 data in red for comparison.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the beginning of the 21st century, the population structure of Andalusia shows a clear inversion of the population pyramid, with the largest cohorts falling between ages 25 and 50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Comparison of the population pyramid in 2008 to that in 1986 shows:</p>
<ol>
<li>A clear decrease in the population under the age of 25, due to a declining birth rate.</li>
<li>An increase in the adult population, as the earlier, larger cohort born in the "baby boom" of the 1960s and 1970s reach adulthood. This effect has been exacerbated by immigration: the largest contingent of immigrants are young adults.</li>
<li>A further increase in the adult population, and especially the older adult population, due to increased <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>.</li>
</ol>
<p>As far as composition by sex, two aspects stand out: the higher percentage of women in the elderly population, owing to women's longer life expectancy, and, on the other hand, the higher percentage of men of working age, due in large part to a predominantly male immigrant population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pob_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-pob-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, 5.35 percent of the population of Andalusia were born outside of Spain. This is a relatively low number for a Spanish region, the national average being three percentage points higher. The immigrants are not evenly distributed among the Andalusian provinces: Almería, with a 15.20 percent immigrant population, is third among all provinces in Spain, while at the other extreme Jaén is only 2.07 percent immigrants and Córdoba 1.77 percent. The predominant nationalities among the immigrant populations are <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a> (92,500, constituting 17.79 percent of the foreigners living in Andalusia) and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> (15.25 percent across the region). When comparing regions rather than individual countries, the single largest immigrant block is from <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, outnumbering either North Africans or non-Spanish Western Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Demographically, this group has provided an important addition to the Andalusian labor force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indicadores_sociales_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Indicadores_sociales-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pob_Extranjera_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pob_Extranjera-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Andalusia is traditionally an agricultural area, but the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">service sector</a> (particularly tourism, retail sales, and transportation) now predominates. The once booming construction sector, hit hard by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">2009 recession</a>, was also important to the region's economy. The industrial sector is less developed than most other regions in Spain.</p>
<p>Between 2000–2006 economic growth per annum was 3.72%, one of the highest in the country. Still, according to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_(Spain)" title="Instituto Nacional de Estadística (Spain)">Instituto Nacional de Estadística</a> (INE), the GDP per capita of Andalusia (€17,401; 2006) remains the second lowest in Spain, with only <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> lagging behind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_sector">Primary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Primary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_sector" title="Primary sector">primary sector</a>, despite adding the least of the three sectors to the regional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> remains important, especially when compared to typical developed economies. The primary sector produces 8.26 percent of regional GDP and employs 8.19 percent of the workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In monetary terms it could be considered a rather uncompetitive sector, given its level of productivity compared to other Spanish regions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In addition to its numeric importance relative to other regions, agriculture and other primary sector activities have strong roots in local culture and identity.</p>
<p>The primary sector is divided into a number of subsectors: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">commercial fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture.2C_husbandry.2C_hunting.2C_and_forestry">Agriculture, husbandry, hunting, and forestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Agriculture, husbandry, hunting, and forestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="548" data-file-width="947" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg/325px-Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg/488px-Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg/650px-Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg.png 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aceites_DOP_Andaluc%C3%ADa.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protected_Geographical_Status" title="Protected Geographical Status">Denominations of origin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a> in Andalusia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For many centuries, Andalusian society was mainly agricultural. Even today, 45.74 percent of the Andalusian territory is cultivated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The primary cultivation is dryland farming of <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunflower" title="Sunflower">sunflowers</a> without artificial <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a>, especially in the vast countryside of the Guadalquivir valley and the high plains of Granada and Almería-with a considerably lesser and more geographically focused cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avena" title="Avena">oats</a>. Using irrigation, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> are also grown on the banks of the Guadalquivir and <a href="/wiki/Genil" title="Genil">Genil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg/220px-Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg/330px-Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg/440px-Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olivares_en_Ja%C3%A9n.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Olive orchards in <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1os_de_la_Encina" title="Baños de la Encina">Baños de la Encina</a> province of Jaén.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most important tree crops are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olea_europaea" title="Olea europaea">olives</a>, especially in the Subbetic regions of the provinces of Córdoba and Jáen, where irrigated olive orchards constitute a large component of agricultural output.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> There are extensive <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a> in various zones such as <a href="/wiki/Jerez_de_la_Frontera" title="Jerez de la Frontera">Jerez de la Frontera</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sherry" title="Sherry">sherry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Condado_de_Huelva" title="Condado de Huelva">Condado de Huelva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montilla-Moriles" title="Montilla-Moriles">Montilla-Moriles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaga_(wine)" title="Malaga (wine)">Málaga</a>. Fruits—mainly <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> fruits—are grown near the banks of the Guadalquivir; <a href="/wiki/Almond" title="Almond">almonds</a>, which require far less water, are grown on the high plains of Granada and Almería.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In monetary terms, by far the most productive and competitive agriculture in Andalusia is the intensive forced cultivation of strawberries, raspberries, blueberries, and other fruits grown under hothouse conditions under clear plastic, often in sandy zones, on the coasts, in Almería and Huelva.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_(Huelva).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg/220px-Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg/330px-Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg/440px-Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_%28Huelva%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dehesa_Boyal._Bollullos_Par_del_Condado_(Huelva).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Dehesa Boyal</i> (meadow for grazing animals), <a href="/wiki/Bollullos_Par_del_Condado" title="Bollullos Par del Condado">Bollullos Par del Condado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">Huelva</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">Organic farming</a> has recently undergone rapid expansion in Andalusia, mainly for export to European markets but with increasing demand developing in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Andalusia has a long tradition of <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> farming, but it is now restricted mainly to mountain meadows, where there is less pressure from other potential uses. Andalusians have a long and colourful history of <a href="/wiki/Dog_breeding" title="Dog breeding">dog breeding</a> that can be observed throughout the region today. The raising of livestock now plays a semi-marginal role in the Andalusian economy, constituting only 15 percent of the primary sector, half the number for Spain taken as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Extensive" raising of livestock grazes the animals on natural or cultivated <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pastures</a>, whereas "intensive" raising of livestock is based in <a href="/wiki/Fodder" title="Fodder">fodder</a> rather than pasture. Although the productivity is higher than with extensive techniques, the economics are quite different. While intensive techniques now dominate in Europe and even in other regions of Spain, most of Andalusia's <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, virtually all of its <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goats</a>, and a good portion of its <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pigs</a> are raised by extensive farming in mountain pastures. This includes the <a href="/wiki/Black_Iberian_pig" title="Black Iberian pig">Black Iberian pigs</a> that are the source of <i><a href="/wiki/Jam%C3%B3n_ib%C3%A9rico" title="Jamón ibérico">Jamón ibérico</a></i>. Andalusia's native sheep and goats present a great economic opportunity in a Europe where animal products are generally in strong supply, but the sheep and goat meat, milk, and leather (and the products derived from these) are relatively scarce. <a href="/wiki/Dog" title="Dog">Dogs</a> are bred not just as companion animals, but also as herding animals used by goat and sheep herders.</p>
<p>Hunting remains relatively important in Andalusia, but has largely lost its character as a means of obtaining food. It is now more of a leisure activity linked to the mountain areas and complementary to forestry and the raising of livestock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gancaz_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-gancaz-98">[98]</a></sup> Dogs are frequently used as hunting companions to retrieve killed game.</p>
<p>The Andalusian <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a> are important for their extent—50 percent of the territory of Andalusia—and for other less quantifiable environmental reasons, such as their value in preventing erosion, regulating the flow of water necessary for other flora and fauna. For these reasons, there is legislation in place to protect the Andalusian forests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The value of forest products as such constitutes only 2 percent of agricultural production. This comes mostly from cultivated species—<a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> in Huelva and <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">poplar</a> in Granada—as well as naturally occurring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cork_oak" title="Cork oak">cork oak</a> in the Sierra Morena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">Fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG/220px-Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG/330px-Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG/440px-Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muelle_pesquero_de_Algeciras_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fishing port of Algeciras.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">Fishing</a> is a longstanding tradition on the Andalusian coasts. Fish and other seafood have long figured prominently in the local diet and in the local <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomic</a> culture: <a href="/wiki/Fried_fish" title="Fried fish">fried fish</a> (<i>pescaito frito</i> in local dialect), white <a href="/wiki/Prawn" title="Prawn">prawns</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Almadraba" title="Almadraba">almadraba</a></i> tuna, among others. The Andalusian fishing fleet is Spain's second largest, after <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, and Andalusia's 38 fishing ports are the most of any Spanish autonomous community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Commercial fishing produces only 0.5 percent of the product of the regional primary sector by value, but there are areas where it has far greater importance. In the province of Huelva it constitutes 20 percent of the primary sector, and locally in <a href="/wiki/Punta_Umbr%C3%ADa" title="Punta Umbría">Punta Umbría</a> 70 percent of the work force is involved in commercial fishing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Failure to comply with fisheries laws regarding the use of trawling, urban <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> of the seacoast, destruction of habitats by coastal construction (for example, alteration of the mouths of rivers, construction of ports), and diminution of fisheries by <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">overexploitation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> have created a permanent crisis in the Andalusian fisheries, justifying attempts to convert the fishing fleet. The decrease in fish stocks has led to the rise of <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Fish_farming" title="Fish farming">fish farming</a> both on the coasts and in the interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Despite the general poor returns in recent years, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> retains a certain importance in Andalusia. Andalusia produces half of Spain's mining product by value. Of Andalusia's production, roughly half comes from the province of Huelva. Mining for precious metals at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minas_de_Riotinto" title="Minas de Riotinto">Minas de Riotinto</a> in Huelva (<i>see <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto Group</a></i>) dates back to pre-Roman times; the mines were abandoned in the Middle Ages and rediscovered in 1556. Other mining activity is <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> mining in the Guadiato valley in the province of Córdoba; various metals at <a href="/wiki/Aznalc%C3%B3llar" title="Aznalcóllar">Aznalcóllar</a> in the province of Seville, and iron at <a href="/wiki/Alquife" title="Alquife">Alquife</a> in the province of Granada. In addition, limestone, clay, and other materials used in construction are well distributed throughout Andalusia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_sector:_industry">Secondary sector: industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Secondary sector: industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Andalusian industrial sector has always been relatively small. Nevertheless, in 2007, Andalusian industry earned 11.979 million euros and employed more than 290,000 workers. This represented 9.15 percent of regional GDP, far below the 15.08 the secondary sector represents in the economy of Spain as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> By analyzing the different subsectors of the food industry Andalusian industry accounts for more than 16% of total production. In a comparison with the Spanish economy, this subsector is virtually the only food that has some weight in the national economy with 16.16%. Lies far behind the manufacturing sector of shipping materials just over 10% of the Spanish economy. Companies like Cruzcampo (Heineken Group), Puleva, Domecq, Santana Motors or Renault-Andalusia, are exponents of these two subsectors. Of note is the Andalusian aeronautical sector, which is second nationally only behind Madrid and represents approximately 21% of total turnover in terms of employment, highlighting companies like Airbus, Airbus Military, or the newly formed Aerospace Alestis. On the contrary it is symptomatic of how little weight the regional economy in such important sectors such as textiles or electronics at the national level.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Andalusian industry is also characterized by a specialization in industrial activities of transforming raw agricultural and mineral materials. This is largely done by small enterprises without the public or foreign investment more typical of a high level of industrialization.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_sector:_services">Tertiary sector: services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tertiary sector: services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG/220px-Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG/330px-Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG/440px-Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_Sancti_Petri.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Castle of Sancti Petri, located in <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_C%C3%A1diz" title="San Fernando, Cádiz">San Fernando, Cádiz</a>. One of the largest components of the service sector is "sun and sand" tourism.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In recent decades the Andalusian tertiary (service) sector has grown greatly, and has come to constitute the majority of the regional economy, as is typical of contemporary economies in developed nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In 1975 the service sector produced 51.1 percent of local GDP and employed 40.8 percent of the work force. In 2007, this had risen to 67.9 percent of GDP and 66.42 percent of jobs. This process of "tertiarization" of the economy has followed a somewhat unusual course in Andalusia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tertiarization_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-tertiarization-108">[108]</a></sup> This growth occurred somewhat earlier than in most developed economies and occurred independently of the local industrial sector. There were two principal reasons that "tertiarization" followed a different course in Andalusia than elsewhere:</p>
<p>1. Andalusian capital found it impossible to compete in the industrial sector against more developed regions, and was obligated to invest in sectors that were easier to enter.</p>
<p>2. The absence of an industrial sector that could absorb displaced agricultural workers and artisans led to the proliferation of services with rather low productivity. This unequal development compared to other regions led to a hypertrophied and unproductive service sector, which has tended to reinforce underdevelopment, because it has not led to large accumulations of capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tertiarization_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-tertiarization-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_in_Andalusia">Tourism in Andalusia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tourism in Andalusia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rabida1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1750" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Rabida1.jpg/220px-Rabida1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Rabida1.jpg/330px-Rabida1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Rabida1.jpg/440px-Rabida1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rabida1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_R%C3%A1bida_Monastery" title="La Rábida Monastery">La Rábida Monastery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palos_de_la_Frontera" title="Palos de la Frontera">Palos de la Frontera</a>, province of Huelva.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="981" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg/220px-Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg/330px-Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg/440px-Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ronda_La_Ciudad2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of <a href="/wiki/Ronda" title="Ronda">Ronda</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:01_Antequera,_Andalusia,_Spain.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg/220px-01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg/330px-01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg/440px-01_Antequera%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:01_Antequera,_Andalusia,_Spain.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal Collegiate Church of Santa María la Mayor in <a href="/wiki/Antequera" title="Antequera">Antequera</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due in part to the relatively mild winter and spring climate, the south of Spain is attractive to overseas visitors–especially tourists from Northern Europe. While inland areas such as <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Ja%C3%A9n_(Spain)" title="Province of Jaén (Spain)">Jaén</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba_(Spanish_province)" title="Córdoba (Spanish province)">Córdoba</a> and the hill villages and towns remain relatively untouched by tourism, the coastal areas of Andalusia have heavy visitor traffic for much of the year.</p>
<p>Among the autonomous communities, Andalusia is second only to <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> in tourism, with nearly 30 million visitors every year. The principal tourist destinations in Andalusia are the <a href="/wiki/Costa_del_Sol" title="Costa del Sol">Costa del Sol</a> and (secondarily) the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada (Spain)">Sierra Nevada</a>. As discussed <a href="#Climate">above</a>, Andalusia is one of the sunniest and warmest places in Europe, making it a center of "sun and sand" tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> 70 percent of the lodging capacity and 75 percent of the nights booked in Andalusian hotels are in coastal municipalities. The largest number of tourists come in August—13.26 percent of the nights booked throughout the year—and the smallest number in December—5.36 percent.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PuertoBanus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6070" data-file-width="4047" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/PuertoBanus.jpg/170px-PuertoBanus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/PuertoBanus.jpg/255px-PuertoBanus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/PuertoBanus.jpg/340px-PuertoBanus.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PuertoBanus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ban%C3%BAs" title="Puerto Banús">Puerto Banús</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Marbella" title="Marbella">Marbella</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the west (Atlantic) coast are the <a href="/wiki/Costa_de_la_Luz" title="Costa de la Luz">Costa de la Luz</a> (provinces of Huelva and Cádiz), and on the east (Mediterranean) coast, the <a href="/wiki/Costa_del_Sol" title="Costa del Sol">Costa del Sol</a> (provinces of Cádiz y Málaga), <a href="/wiki/Costa_Tropical" title="Costa Tropical">Costa Tropical</a> (Granada and part of Almería) and the <a href="/wiki/Costa_de_Almer%C3%ADa" title="Costa de Almería">Costa de Almería</a>. In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Flag_beach" title="Blue Flag beach">Blue Flag beach</a> program of the non-profit <a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Environmental_Education" title="Foundation for Environmental Education">Foundation for Environmental Education</a> recognized 66 Andalusian beaches and 18 pleasure craft ports as being in a good state of conservation in terms of sustainability, accessibility, and quality.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Nonetheless, the level of tourism on the Andalusian coasts has been high enough to have a significant environmental impact, and other organizations—such as the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Ecologists_in_Action" title="Ecologists in Action">Ecologists in Action</a> (<i>Ecologistas en Acción</i>) with their description of "Black Flag beaches"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>—have expressed the opposite sentiment. However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hotel_chains" title="Hotel chains">Hotel chains</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Fuerte_Hotels#Responsible_Tourism" title="Fuerte Hotels">Fuerte Hotels</a> have ensured that sustainability within the tourism industry is one of their highest priorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Together with "sand and sun" tourism, there has also been a strong increase in nature tourism in the interior, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">cultural tourism</a>, sport tourism, and conventions<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. One example of sport and nature tourism is the ski resort at <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_National_Park_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada National Park (Spain)">Sierra Nevada National Park</a>.</p>
<p>As for cultural tourism, Andalusia has some notable monuments dating back to the Muslim era: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Great Mosque of Córdoba">Great Mosque of Córdoba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra" title="Alhambra">Alhambra</a> in Granada, the <a href="/wiki/Giralda" title="Giralda">Giralda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcazar</a> in Seville, and the <a href="/wiki/Alcazaba_of_M%C3%A1laga" title="Alcazaba of Málaga">Alcazaba</a> in Málaga. There are hundreds of cultural tourist destinations: cathedrals, castles, forts, monasteries, and historic city centers; the city centers of <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Abeda" title="Úbeda">Úbeda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baeza" title="Baeza">Baeza</a> in the province of Jaén are UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>.</p>
<p>Each of the provinces shows a great variety of architectural styles: <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a> and more modern styles. Further, there are the <i><a href="/wiki/Lugares_colombinos" title="Lugares colombinos">Lugares colombinos</a></i>, significant places in the life of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Palos_de_la_Frontera" title="Palos de la Frontera">Palos de la Frontera</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_R%C3%A1bida_Monastery" title="La Rábida Monastery">La Rábida Monastery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moguer" title="Moguer">Moguer</a>) in the province of Huelva. There are also archeological sites of great interest: the Roman city of <a href="/wiki/Italica" title="Italica">Italica</a>, birthplace of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Emperor" title="Roman Emperor">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a> and (most likely) <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>; <a href="/wiki/Baelo_Claudia" title="Baelo Claudia">Baelo Claudia</a> near the Straits of Gibraltar; <a href="/wiki/Medina_Azahara" title="Medina Azahara">Medina Azahara</a>, the city-palace of the Cordoban <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">caliph</a> <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_III" title="Abd-ar-Rahman III">Abd-ar-Rahman III</a>, where major excavations still continue.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg/220px-Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg/330px-Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg/440px-Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Playas_de_Nerja_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Nerja" title="Nerja">Nerja</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Andalusia was the birthplace of such great painters as <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Diego Velázquez">Velázquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Esteban_Murillo" title="Bartolomé Esteban Murillo">Murillo</a> (Seville) and, more recently, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Picasso</a> (Málaga); Picasso is memorialized by his native city at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Picasso_M%C3%A1laga" title="Museo Picasso Málaga">Museo Picasso Málaga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fundaci%C3%B3n_Picasso" title="Fundación Picasso">Natal House Foundation</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Murillo" title="Casa de Murillo">Casa de Murillo</a> was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_museum" title="House museum">house museum</a> 1982–1998, but is now mostly offices for the Andalusian Council of Culture. The <a class="external text" href="http://www.cacmalaga.org/" rel="nofollow">CAC Málaga (Museum of Modern Art)</a> is the most visited museum of Andalusia<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>and has offered exhibitions of artists such as <a href="/wiki/Louise_Bourgeois" title="Louise Bourgeois">Louise Bourgeois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jake_and_Dinos_Chapman" title="Jake and Dinos Chapman">Jake and Dinos Chapman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Richter" title="Gerhard Richter">Gerhard Richter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anish_Kapoor" title="Anish Kapoor">Anish Kapoor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Mueck" title="Ron Mueck">Ron Mueck</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Graham" title="Rodney Graham">Rodney Graham</a>. Malaga is also located part of the private <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Cervera" title="Carmen Cervera">Carmen Thyssen-Bornemisza Collection</a> at <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Thyssen_Museum" title="Carmen Thyssen Museum">Carmen Thyssen Museum</a>.</p>
<p>There are numerous other significant museums around the region, both of paintings and of archeological artifacts such as gold jewelry, pottery and other ceramics, and other works that demonstrate the region's artisanal traditions.</p>
<p>The Council of Government has designated the following "Municipios Turísticos": in Almería, <a href="/wiki/Roquetas_de_Mar" title="Roquetas de Mar">Roquetas de Mar</a>; in Cádiz, <a href="/wiki/Chiclana_de_la_Frontera" title="Chiclana de la Frontera">Chiclana de la Frontera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chipiona" title="Chipiona">Chipiona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conil_de_la_Frontera" title="Conil de la Frontera">Conil de la Frontera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grazalema" title="Grazalema">Grazalema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rota,_Andalusia" title="Rota, Andalusia">Rota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">Tarifa</a>; in Granada, <a href="/wiki/Almu%C3%B1%C3%A9car" title="Almuñécar">Almuñécar</a>; in Huelva, <a href="/wiki/Aracena" title="Aracena">Aracena</a>; in Jaén, <a href="/wiki/Cazorla" title="Cazorla">Cazorla</a>; in Málaga, <a href="/wiki/Benalm%C3%A1dena" title="Benalmádena">Benalmádena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuengirola" title="Fuengirola">Fuengirola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nerja" title="Nerja">Nerja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n_de_la_Victoria" title="Rincón de la Victoria">Rincón de la Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronda" title="Ronda">Ronda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Torremolinos" title="Torremolinos">Torremolinos</a>; in Seville, <a href="/wiki/Santiponce" title="Santiponce">Santiponce</a>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Monuments_and_features">Monuments and features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Monuments and features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>

<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cueva_de_Menga" title="Cueva de Menga">Cueva de Menga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antequera" title="Antequera">Antequera (Málaga)</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="299" data-file-width="500" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG/325px-Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG/488px-Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carreteras_en_Andaluc%C3%ADa.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
First order roads of Andalusia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As in any modern society, transport systems are an essential structural element of the functioning of Andalusia. The transportation network facilitates territorial coordination, economic development and distribution, and intercity transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infra_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-infra-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In urban transport, underdeveloped public transport systems put pedestrian traffic and other non-motorized traffic are at a disadvantage compared to the use of private vehicles. Several Andalusian capitals—Córdoba, Granada and Seville—have recently been trying to remedy this by strengthening their public transport systems and providing a better infrastructure for the use of <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">bicycles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg/220px-Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg/330px-Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg/440px-Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sevilla2005Julio_050.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Estación de Santa Justa, Sevilla</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For over a century, the conventional rail network has been centralized on the regional capital, Seville, and the national capital, Madrid; in general, there are no direct connections between provincial capitals. High-speed <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> trains run from Madrid via Córdoba to Seville and Málaga. Further AVE routes are under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The Madrid-Córdoba-Seville route was the first high-velocity route in Spain (operating since 1992). Other principal routes are the one from Algeciras to Seville and from <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">Almería</a> via Granada to Madrid.</p>
<p>Most of the principal roads have been converted into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limited_access_highway" title="Limited access highway">limited access highways</a> known as <i><a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa" title="Autovía">autovías</a></i>. The Autovía del Este (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-4" title="Autovía A-4">Autovía A-4</a>) runs from Madrid through the Despeñaperros Natural Park, then via Bailén, Córdoba, and Seville to Cádiz, and is part of <a href="/wiki/European_route_E05" title="European route E05">European route E05</a> in the <a href="/wiki/International_E-road_network" title="International E-road network">International E-road network</a>. The other main road in the region is the portion of <a href="/wiki/European_route_E15" title="European route E15">European route E15</a>, which runs as the Autovia del Mediterráneo along the Spanish Mediterranean coast. Parts of this constitute the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superhighway" title="Superhighway">superhighway</a> <a href="/wiki/Autopista_AP-7" title="Autopista AP-7">Autopista AP-7</a>, while in other areas it is <a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-7" title="Autovía A-7">Autovía A-7</a>. Both of these roads run generally east-west, although the Autovía A-4 turns to the south in western Andalusia.</p>
<p>Other first-order roads include the <a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-48" title="Autovía A-48">Autovía A-48</a> roughly along the Atlantic coast from Cádiz to Algeciras, continuing European route E05 to meet up with <a href="/wiki/European_route_E15" title="European route E15">European route E15</a>; the Autovía del Quinto Centenario (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-49" title="Autovía A-49">Autovía A-49</a>), which continues west from Seville (where the Autovía A-4 turns toward the south) and goes on to Huelva and into Portugal as <a href="/wiki/European_route_E01" title="European route E01">European route E01</a>; the Autovía Ruta de la Plata (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-66" title="Autovía A-66">Autovía A-66</a>), <a href="/wiki/European_route_E803" title="European route E803">European route E803</a>, which roughly corresponds to the ancient Roman '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Route" title="Silver Route">Silver Route</a>' from the mines of northern Spain, and runs north from Seville; the Autovía de Málaga (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-45" title="Autovía A-45">Autovía A-45</a>), which runs south from Córdoba to Málaga; and the Autovía de Sierra Nevada (<a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-44" title="Autovía A-44">Autovía A-44</a>), part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_route_E902" title="European route E902">European route E902</a>, which runs south from Jaén to the Mediterranean coast at Motril.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="2306" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg/220px-Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg/330px-Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg/440px-Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_de_Malaga.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="Málaga Airport">Málaga Airport</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2008 Andalusia has six public airports, all of which can legally handle international flights; however the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="Málaga Airport">Málaga Airport</a> is dominant, handling 60.67 percent of passengers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Datos_Aena_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Datos_Aena-120">[120]</a></sup> and 85 percent of its international traffic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Seville_Airport" title="Seville Airport">Seville Airport</a> handles another 20.12 percent of traffic, and the <a href="/wiki/Jerez_Airport" title="Jerez Airport">Jerez Airport</a> 7.17 percent, so that these three airports account for 87.96 percent of traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Datos_Aena_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Datos_Aena-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Málaga Airport is the international airport that offers a wide variety of international destinations. It has a daily link with twenty cities in Spain and over a hundred cities in Europe (mainly in Great Britain, Central Europe and the Nordic countries but also the main cities of Eastern Europe: <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>), North Africa, Middle East (<a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>) and North America (<a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Algeciras.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Port_of_Algeciras.jpg/220px-Port_of_Algeciras.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Port_of_Algeciras.jpg/330px-Port_of_Algeciras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Port_of_Algeciras.jpg/440px-Port_of_Algeciras.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Algeciras.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Port_of_Algeciras" title="Port of Algeciras">Port of Algeciras</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main ports are Algeciras (for freight and container traffic) and Málaga for cruise ships. Algeciras is Spain's leading commercial port, with 60,000,000 tonnes (66,000,000 short tons) of cargo in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Seville has Spain's only commercial river port. Other significant commercial ports in Andalusia are the ports of the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Bay of Cádiz">Bay of Cádiz</a>, Almería and Huelva.</p>
<p>The Council of Government has approved a Plan of Infrastructures for the Sustainability of Transport in Andalusia (PISTA) 2007–2013, which plans an investment of 30 billion euros during that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_infrastructure">Energy infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Energy infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The lack of high-quality <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> in Andalusia has led to a strong dependency on <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> imports. Still, Andalusia has a strong potential for the development of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>, above all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_energy" title="Wind energy">wind energy</a>. The Andalusian Energy Agency established in 2005 by the autonomous government, is a new governmental organ charged with the development of energy policy and provision of a sufficient supply of energy for the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infra_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-infra-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>The infrastructure for production of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> consists of eight large <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">thermal power stations</a>, more than 70 <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> power plants, two <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farms</a>, and 14 major <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">cogeneration</a> facilities. Historically, the largest Andalusian business in this sector was the <a href="/wiki/Compa%C3%B1%C3%ADa_Sevillana_de_Electricidad" title="Compañía Sevillana de Electricidad">Compañía Sevillana de Electricidad</a>, founded in 1894, absorbed into <a href="/wiki/Endesa_(Spain)" title="Endesa (Spain)">Endesa</a> in 1996.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="1024" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg/220px-PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg/330px-PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg/440px-PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PS10_solar_power_tower_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Solar_power_tower" title="Solar power tower">Solar power tower</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS10_solar_power_tower" title="PS10 solar power tower">PS10</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sanl%C3%BAcar_la_Mayor" title="Sanlúcar la Mayor">Sanlúcar la Mayor</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_tower" title="Solar power tower">Solar power tower</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS10_solar_power_tower" title="PS10 solar power tower">PS10</a> was built by the Andalusian firm <a href="/wiki/Abengoa" title="Abengoa">Abengoa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sanl%C3%BAcar_la_Mayor" title="Sanlúcar la Mayor">Sanlúcar la Mayor</a> in the province of Seville, and began operating in March 2007. It is the largest existing solar power facility in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Smaller solar power stations, also recent, exist at <a href="/wiki/C%C3%BAllar" title="Cúllar">Cúllar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galera,_Granada" title="Galera, Granada">Galera, Granada</a>, inaugurated by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Geosol&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Geosol (page does not exist)">Geosol</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Caja_Granada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Caja Granada (page does not exist)">Caja Granada</a>. Two more large thermosolar facilities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andasol" title="Andasol">Andasol I y II</a>, planned at Hoya de <a href="/wiki/Guadix" title="Guadix">Guadix</a> in the province of Granada are expected to supply electricity to half a million households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andasol2_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andasol2-124">[124]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plataforma_Solar_de_Almer%C3%ADa" title="Plataforma Solar de Almería">Plataforma Solar de Almería</a> (PSA) in the Tabernas Desert is an important center for the exploration of the solar energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest wind power firm in the region is the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sociedad_E%C3%B3lica_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sociedad Eólica de Andalucía (page does not exist)">Sociedad Eólica de Andalucía</a>, formed by the merger of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Planta_E%C3%B3lica_del_Sur_S.A.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Planta Eólica del Sur S.A. (page does not exist)">Planta Eólica del Sur S.A.</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Energ%C3%ADa_E%C3%B3lica_del_Estrecho_S.A.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Energía Eólica del Estrecho S.A. (page does not exist)">Energía Eólica del Estrecho S.A.</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portadafacultad.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Portadafacultad.gif/220px-Portadafacultad.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Portadafacultad.gif/330px-Portadafacultad.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Portadafacultad.gif/440px-Portadafacultad.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portadafacultad.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Law School of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Granada" title="University of Granada">University of Granada</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As throughout Spain, basic education in Andalusia is free and compulsory. Students are required to complete ten years of schooling, and may not leave school before the age of 16, after which students may continue on to a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">baccalaureate</a>, to intermediate <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education</a>, to intermediate-level schooling in arts and design, to intermediate sports studies, or to the working world.</p>
<p>Andalusia has a tradition of higher education dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Madrasah_of_Granada" title="Madrasah of Granada">Madrasah of Granada</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Baeza" title="University of Baeza">University of Baeza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Osuna" title="University of Osuna">University of Osuna</a>.</p>
<p>As of 2009, there are ten private or public universities in Andalucia. University studies are structured in cycles, awarding degrees based on <a href="/wiki/European_Credit_Transfer_and_Accumulation_System" title="European Credit Transfer and Accumulation System">ECTS credits</a> in accord with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bologna_process" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>, which the Andalusian universities are adopting in accord with the other universities of the <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="862" data-file-width="1291" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png/325px-Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png/488px-Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png/650px-Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_sanitario_de_Andaluc%C3%ADa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Healthcare districts of Andalusia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Responsibility for healthcare jurisdictions devolved from the Spanish government to Andalusia with the enactment of the Statute of Autonomy. Thus, the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Health_Service" title="Andalusian Health Service">Andalusian Health Service</a> (<i>Servicio Andaluz de Salud</i>) currently manages almost all public health resources of the Community, with such exceptions as health resources for prisoners and members of the military, which remain under central administration.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andalusia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the Outreach Program for Science in Andalusia, Andalusia contributes 14 percent of Spain's scientific production behind only Madrid and Catalonia among the autonomous communities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> even though regional investment in <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> (R&amp;D) as a proportion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> is below the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The lack of research capacity in business and the low participation of the private sector in research has resulted in R&amp;D taking place largely in the public sector.</p>
<p>The Council of Innovation, Science and Business is the organ of the autonomous government responsible for universities, research, technological development, industry, and energy. The council coordinates and initiates scientific and technical innovation through specialized centers an initiatives such as the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Center_for_Marine_Science_and_Technology" title="Andalusian Center for Marine Science and Technology">Andalusian Center for Marine Science and Technology</a> (<i>Centro Andaluz de Ciencia y Tecnología Marina</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Technological_Corporation_of_Andalusia" title="Technological Corporation of Andalusia">Technological Corporation of Andalusia</a> (<i>Corporación Tecnológica de Andalucía</i>).</p>
